   <h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Lesotho</h1> 
   <div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content"> 
    <div id="siteSub" class="noprint">
     From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia
    </div> 
    <div id="contentSub"></div> 
    <div id="contentSub2"></div> 
    <div id="jump-to-nav"></div> <a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a> <a class="mw-jump-link" href="#searchInput">Jump to search</a> 
    <div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr">
     <div class="mw-parser-output">
      <div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">
       Landlocked country forming an enclave in South Africa
      </div>

      <p><b>Lesotho</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="'l' in 'lie'">l</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span><span title="/uː/: 'oo' in 'goose'">uː</span><span title="'t' in 'tie'">t</span><span title="/uː/: 'oo' in 'goose'">uː</span></span>/</a></span> <span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:Lesotho.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20"></a></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/79/Lesotho.ogg" class="internal" title="Lesotho.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span></span>,<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> <small>Sotho pronunciation:&nbsp;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">[lɪˈsʊːtʰʊ]</a></span>), officially the <b>Kingdom of Lesotho</b> (<a href="/wiki/Sotho_language" title="Sotho language">Sotho</a>: <i lang="st">'Muso oa Lesotho</i>), is an <a href="/wiki/Enclave_and_exclave" title="Enclave and exclave">enclaved country</a> within the border of <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a>. It is by far the largest of the world's <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_that_border_only_one_other_country#Landlocked" title="List of countries that border only one other country">three independent states completely surrounded by the territory of another country</a>; with <a href="/wiki/Vatican_City" title="Vatican City">Vatican City</a> and <a href="/wiki/San_Marino" title="San Marino">San Marino</a> being the other two. Additionally, it is the only such state outside the Italian peninsula, and the only one that is not a <a href="/wiki/Microstate" title="Microstate">microstate</a>. Lesotho is just over 30,000&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (11,583&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi) and has a population of around 2 million. Its capital and largest city is <a href="/wiki/Maseru" title="Maseru">Maseru</a>. The official language is <a href="/wiki/Sesotho_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Sesotho language">Sesotho</a>. </p>
      <p>Lesotho was previously the <a href="/wiki/British_Crown_Colony" class="mw-redirect" title="British Crown Colony">British Crown Colony</a> of <a href="/wiki/Basutoland" title="Basutoland">Basutoland</a>, but it declared independence from the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> on 4 October 1966. It is now a fully <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_state" title="Sovereign state">sovereign state</a> and is a member of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth of Nations</a>, the <a href="/wiki/African_Union" title="African Union">African Union</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Southern_African_Development_Community" title="Southern African Development Community">Southern African Development Community</a> (SADC). The name <i>Lesotho</i> roughly translates to "the land of the people who speak Sesotho".<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lesotho&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Lesotho" title="History of Lesotho">History of Lesotho</a>
      </div> 
      <table class="box-More_citations_needed_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">

      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">

      <p>The original inhabitants of Lesotho were the <a href="/wiki/San_people" title="San people">San people</a>. Examples of their <a href="/wiki/San_rock_art" title="San rock art">rock art</a> can be found in the mountains throughout the area.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span id="Rule_of_Moshoeshoe_I_.281822.E2.80.931868.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Rule_of_Moshoeshoe_I_(1822–1868)">Rule of Moshoeshoe I (1822–1868)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lesotho&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Rule of Moshoeshoe I (1822–1868)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Modern Lesotho, then called Basutoland, emerged as a single <a href="/wiki/Body_politic" title="Body politic">polity</a> under King <a href="/wiki/Moshoeshoe_I" title="Moshoeshoe I">Moshoeshoe I</a> in 1822. Moshoeshoe, a son of Mokhachane, a minor <a href="/wiki/Tribal_chief" title="Tribal chief">chief</a> of the Bakoteli lineage, formed his own <a href="/wiki/Clan" title="Clan">clan</a> and became a chief around 1804. Between 1820 and 1823, he and his followers settled at the <a href="/wiki/Butha-Buthe" title="Butha-Buthe">Butha-Buthe</a> Mountain, joining with former adversaries in resistance against the <a href="/wiki/Mfecane" title="Mfecane">Lifaqane</a> associated with the reign of <a href="/wiki/Shaka_Zulu" class="mw-redirect" title="Shaka Zulu">Shaka Zulu</a> from 1818 to 1828. </p>
      <p>Further evolution of the state emerged from conflicts between <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British</a> and <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Dutch</a> colonists leaving the <a href="/wiki/British_Cape_Colony" class="mw-redirect" title="British Cape Colony">Cape Colony</a> following its seizure from the French-allied Dutch by the British in 1795, and also from the <a href="/wiki/Orange_River_Sovereignty" title="Orange River Sovereignty">Orange River Sovereignty</a> and subsequent <a href="/wiki/Orange_Free_State" title="Orange Free State">Orange Free State</a>. <a href="/wiki/Missionaries" class="mw-redirect" title="Missionaries">Missionaries</a> Thomas Arbousset, Eugène Casalis and Constant Gosselin from the <a href="/wiki/Paris_Evangelical_Missionary_Society" title="Paris Evangelical Missionary Society">Paris Evangelical Missionary Society</a>, invited by Moshoeshoe I, were placed at <a href="/wiki/Morija" title="Morija">Morija</a>, developing Sesotho <a href="/wiki/Orthography" title="Orthography">orthography</a> and printed works in the <a href="/wiki/Sesotho_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Sesotho language">Sesotho language</a> between 1837 and 1855. Casalis, acting as translator and providing advice on foreign affairs, helped set up diplomatic channels and acquire guns for use against the encroaching Europeans and the <a href="/wiki/Griqua_people" title="Griqua people">Griqua people</a>. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Trekboer" class="mw-redirect" title="Trekboer">Trekboers</a> from the Cape Colony arrived on the western borders of <a href="/wiki/Basutoland" title="Basutoland">Basutoland</a> and claimed rights to its land, the first of which being Jan de Winnaar, who settled in the <a href="/wiki/Matlakeng" class="mw-redirect" title="Matlakeng">Matlakeng</a> area in May–June 1838. Incoming <a href="/wiki/Boers" class="mw-redirect" title="Boers">Boers</a> attempted to colonise the land between the two rivers and even north of the <a href="/wiki/Caledon_River" title="Caledon River">Caledon</a>, claiming that it had been abandoned by the Sotho people. Moshoeshoe subsequently signed a treaty with the British Governor of the Cape Colony, Sir <a href="/wiki/George_Thomas_Napier" title="George Thomas Napier">George Thomas Napier</a>, that annexed the Orange River Sovereignty where many Boers had settled. These outraged Boers were suppressed in a brief skirmish in 1848. In 1851, a British force was defeated by the Basotho army at Kolonyama, provoking an embarrassing war for the British. After repelling another British attack in 1852, Moshoeshoe sent an appeal to the British commander that settled the dispute diplomatically, and then defeated the Batlokoa in 1853. In 1854, the British pulled out of the region, and in 1858, Moshoeshoe fought a series of wars with the Boers in what is known as the <a href="/wiki/Free_State%E2%80%93Basotho_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Free State–Basotho War">Free State–Basotho War</a>. As a result, Moshoeshoe lost a great portion of the western lowlands. The last war with the Boers ended in 1867 when Moshoeshoe appealed to <a href="/wiki/Queen_Victoria" title="Queen Victoria">Queen Victoria</a>, who agreed to make Basutoland a British <a href="/wiki/Protectorate" title="Protectorate">protectorate</a> in 1868. </p> 
      <h3><span id="British_rule_.281869.E2.80.931966.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="British_rule_(1869–1966)">British rule (1869–1966)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lesotho&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: British rule (1869–1966)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In 1869, the British signed a treaty at <a href="/wiki/Aliwal_North" title="Aliwal North">Aliwal North</a> with the Boers that defined the boundaries of Basutoland. This treaty effectively reduced Moshoeshoe's kingdom to half its previous size by ceding away its western territories. </p>
      <p>Following the <a href="/wiki/Cession" title="Cession">cession</a> in 1869, the British transferred functions from Moshoeshoe's capital in <a href="/wiki/Thaba_Bosiu" title="Thaba Bosiu">Thaba Bosiu</a> to a police camp on the northwest border, <a href="/wiki/Maseru" title="Maseru">Maseru</a>, until eventually the administration of Basutoland was transferred to the Cape Colony in 1871. Moshoeshoe died on 11 March 1870, marking the end of the traditional era and the beginning of the colonial era of Basutoland. He was buried at Thaba Bosiu. </p>
      <p>In the Cape Colony period between 1871 and 1884, Basutoland was treated similarly to other territories that had been forcibly annexed, much to the humiliation of the Basotho, leading to the <a href="/wiki/Basuto_Gun_War" title="Basuto Gun War">Basuto Gun War</a> in 1880–1881.<sup id="cite_ref-cities_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cities-11">[11]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 1884, the territory became a <a href="/wiki/Crown_colony" title="Crown colony">Crown colony</a> by the name of <a href="/wiki/Basutoland" title="Basutoland">Basutoland</a>, with Maseru as its capital. It remained under direct rule by a <a href="/wiki/Governor" title="Governor">governor</a>, though effective internal power was wielded by traditional <a href="/wiki/Tribal_chief" title="Tribal chief">tribal chiefs</a>. In 1905, a <a href="/wiki/Maseru_branch_line" title="Maseru branch line">railway line</a> was built to connect Maseru to the railway network of South Africa. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:1959_Basutoland_National_Council_stamps.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/1959_Basutoland_National_Council_stamps.jpg/220px-1959_Basutoland_National_Council_stamps.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="86" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/1959_Basutoland_National_Council_stamps.jpg/330px-1959_Basutoland_National_Council_stamps.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/1959_Basutoland_National_Council_stamps.jpg/440px-1959_Basutoland_National_Council_stamps.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2702" data-file-height="1059"></a>

        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <h3><span id="Independence_.281966.E2.80.93present.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Independence_(1966–present)">Independence (1966–present)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lesotho&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Independence (1966–present)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_Lesotho_(1966%E2%80%931987).svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Flag_of_Lesotho_%281966%E2%80%931987%29.svg/220px-Flag_of_Lesotho_%281966%E2%80%931987%29.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Flag_of_Lesotho_%281966%E2%80%931987%29.svg/330px-Flag_of_Lesotho_%281966%E2%80%931987%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Flag_of_Lesotho_%281966%E2%80%931987%29.svg/440px-Flag_of_Lesotho_%281966%E2%80%931987%29.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="400"></a>

       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Basutoland gained its independence from the United Kingdom and became the Kingdom of Lesotho in 1966.<sup id="cite_ref-hansenvaa_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hansenvaa-13">[13]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In January 1970, the ruling <a href="/wiki/Basotho_National_Party" title="Basotho National Party">Basotho National Party</a> (BNP) lost the <a href="/wiki/1970_Lesotho_general_election" title="1970 Lesotho general election">first post-independence general elections</a>, with 23 seats to the Basotho Congress Party's (BCP) 36. Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Leabua_Jonathan" title="Leabua Jonathan">Leabua Jonathan</a> refused to cede power to the BCP, instead declaring himself <i>Tona Kholo</i> (Sesotho: 'prime minister'), and imprisoning the BCP leadership. </p>
      <p>BCP began a <a href="/wiki/Rebellion" title="Rebellion">rebellion</a> and then received training in <a href="/wiki/History_of_Libya_under_Muammar_Gaddafi#Libyan_Arab_Republic" title="History of Libya under Muammar Gaddafi">Libya</a> for its <a href="/wiki/Lesotho_Liberation_Army" title="Lesotho Liberation Army">Lesotho Liberation Army</a> (LLA) under the pretense of being <a href="/wiki/Azanian_People%27s_Liberation_Army" title="Azanian People's Liberation Army">Azanian People's Liberation Army</a> (APLA) soldiers of the <a href="/wiki/Pan_Africanist_Congress" class="mw-redirect" title="Pan Africanist Congress">Pan Africanist Congress</a> (PAC). Deprived of arms and supplies by the <a href="/wiki/David_Sibeko" title="David Sibeko">Sibeko</a> faction of the PAC in 1978, the 178-strong LLA was rescued from their <a href="/wiki/Tanzania" title="Tanzania">Tanzanian</a> base by the financial assistance of a <a href="/wiki/Maoism" title="Maoism">Maoist</a> PAC officer, but they launched the <a href="/wiki/Guerrilla_war" class="mw-redirect" title="Guerrilla war">guerrilla war</a> with only a handful of old weapons. The main force was defeated in northern Lesotho, and later guerrillas launched sporadic but usually ineffectual attacks. The campaign was severely compromised when BCP's leader, <a href="/wiki/Ntsu_Mokhehle" title="Ntsu Mokhehle">Ntsu Mokhehle</a>, went to <a href="/wiki/Pretoria" title="Pretoria">Pretoria</a>. In the early 1980s, several Basotho who sympathised with the exiled BCP were threatened with death and attacked by the government of Leabua Jonathan. On 4 September 1981, the family of Benjamin Masilo was attacked. In the attack his 3-year-old grandson died. Exactly four days later, Edgar Mahlomola Motuba, the editor of the popular newspaper <a href="/w/index.php?title=Leselinyana_la_Lesotho&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Leselinyana la Lesotho (page does not exist)">Leselinyana la Lesotho</a>, was abducted from his home together with two friends and murdered. </p>
      <p>The BNP ruled from 1966 until January 1970. What later ensued was a <a href="/wiki/De_facto" title="De facto">de facto</a> government led by Dr. Leabua Jonathan until 1986 when a military <a href="/wiki/Coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="Coup d'état">coup</a> forced it out of office. The Transitional Military Council that came to power granted executive powers to <a href="/wiki/Moshoeshoe_II_of_Lesotho" title="Moshoeshoe II of Lesotho">King Moshoeshoe II</a>, who was until then a <a href="/wiki/Ceremonial_monarch" class="mw-redirect" title="Ceremonial monarch">ceremonial monarch</a>. But in 1987 the King was forced into <a href="/wiki/Exile" title="Exile">exile</a> after coming up with a six-page memorandum on how he wanted the Lesotho's constitution to be, which would have given him more executive powers than the military government had originally agreed to. His son was installed as <a href="/wiki/Letsie_III_of_Lesotho" class="mw-redirect" title="Letsie III of Lesotho">King Letsie III</a> in his place. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Lesotho_mountain_village_(5285775857).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Lesotho_mountain_village_%285285775857%29.jpg/220px-Lesotho_mountain_village_%285285775857%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Lesotho_mountain_village_%285285775857%29.jpg/330px-Lesotho_mountain_village_%285285775857%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Lesotho_mountain_village_%285285775857%29.jpg/440px-Lesotho_mountain_village_%285285775857%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Lesotho_mountain_village_(5285775857).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Lesotho mountain village
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The chairman of the <a href="/wiki/Military_junta" title="Military junta">military junta</a>, Major General <a href="/wiki/Justin_Metsing_Lekhanya" class="mw-redirect" title="Justin Metsing Lekhanya">Justin Metsing Lekhanya</a>, was ousted in 1991 and replaced by Major General <a href="/wiki/Elias_Phisoana_Ramaema" title="Elias Phisoana Ramaema">Elias Phisoana Ramaema</a>, who handed over power to a democratically elected government of the BCP in 1993. Moshoeshoe II returned from exile in 1992 as an ordinary citizen. After the return to democratic government, King Letsie III tried unsuccessfully to persuade the BCP government to reinstate his father (Moshoeshoe II) as <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a>. </p>
      <p>In August 1994, Letsie III staged a military-backed coup that deposed the BCP government, after the BCP government refused to reinstate his father, Moshoeshoe II, according to Lesotho's constitution. The new government did not receive full international recognition. Member states of the <a href="/wiki/Southern_African_Development_Community" title="Southern African Development Community">Southern African Development Community</a> (SADC) engaged in negotiations to reinstate the BCP government. One of the conditions Letsie III put forward for this was that his father should be re-installed as head of state. After protracted negotiations, the BCP government was reinstated and Letsie III abdicated in favour of his father in 1995, but he ascended the throne again when Moshoeshoe II died at the age of fifty-seven in a supposed road accident, when his car plunged off a mountain road during the early hours of 15 January 1996. According to a government statement, Moshoeshoe had set out at 1&nbsp;am to visit his <a href="/wiki/Cattle" title="Cattle">cattle</a> at Matsieng and was returning to <a href="/wiki/Maseru" title="Maseru">Maseru</a> through the <a href="/wiki/Maluti_Mountains" class="mw-redirect" title="Maluti Mountains">Maluti Mountains</a> when his car left the road.<sup id="cite_ref-nyt_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt-14">[14]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 1997, the ruling BCP split over leadership disputes. <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister" class="mw-redirect" title="Prime Minister">Prime Minister</a> <a href="/wiki/Ntsu_Mokhehle" title="Ntsu Mokhehle">Ntsu Mokhehle</a> formed a new party, the <a href="/wiki/Lesotho_Congress_for_Democracy" title="Lesotho Congress for Democracy">Lesotho Congress for Democracy</a> (LCD), and was followed by a majority of members of <a href="/wiki/Parliament" title="Parliament">parliament</a>, which enabled him to form a new government. <a href="/wiki/Pakalitha_Mosisili" title="Pakalitha Mosisili">Pakalitha Mosisili</a> succeeded Mokhehle as party leader and the LCD won the general elections in 1998. Although the elections were pronounced free and fair by local and international observers and a subsequent special commission appointed by SADC, the opposition political parties rejected the results. </p>
      <p>Opposition protests in the country intensified, culminating in a peaceful demonstration outside the royal <a href="/wiki/Palace" title="Palace">palace</a> in August 1998. Exact details of what followed are greatly disputed, both in Lesotho and South Africa. While the <a href="/wiki/Botswana_Defence_Force" title="Botswana Defence Force">Botswana Defence Force</a> troops were welcomed, tensions with <a href="/wiki/South_African_National_Defence_Force" title="South African National Defence Force">South African National Defence Force</a> troops were high, resulting in fighting. Incidences of sporadic <a href="/wiki/Rioting" class="mw-redirect" title="Rioting">rioting</a> intensified when South African troops hoisted a South African flag over the Royal Palace. By the time the SADC forces withdrew in May 1999, much of the capital of <a href="/wiki/Maseru" title="Maseru">Maseru</a> lay in ruins, and the southern provincial capital towns of <a href="/wiki/Mafeteng" title="Mafeteng">Mafeteng</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mohale%27s_Hoek" title="Mohale's Hoek">Mohale's Hoek</a> had lost over a third of their commercial <a href="/wiki/Real_estate" title="Real estate">real estate</a>. A significant number of South Africans and Basotho also died in the fighting. </p>
      <p>An Interim Political Authority (IPA), charged with reviewing the electoral structure in the country, was created in December 1998. The IPA devised a proportional electoral system to ensure that the opposition would be represented in the <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly" title="National Assembly">National Assembly</a>. The new system retained the existing 80 elected Assembly seats, but added 40 seats to be filled on a proportional basis. Elections were held under this new system in May 2002, and the LCD won again, gaining 54 percent of the vote. But for the first time, opposition <a href="/wiki/Political_parties" class="mw-redirect" title="Political parties">political parties</a> won significant numbers of seats, and despite some irregularities and threats of violence from Major General Lekhanya, Lesotho experienced its first peaceful election. Nine opposition parties now hold all 40 of the proportional seats, with the BNP having the largest share (21). The LCD has 79 of the 80 <a href="/wiki/Constituency" class="mw-redirect" title="Constituency">constituency</a>-based seats. Although its elected members participate in the National Assembly, the BNP has launched several legal challenges to the elections, including a recount; none has been successful. </p>
      <p>On 30 August 2014, an alleged abortive military "coup" took place, forcing then Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Thabane" class="mw-redirect" title="Thomas Thabane">Thomas Thabane</a> to flee to South Africa for three days.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> On May 19 2020, Thomas Thabane formally stepped down as prime minister of Lesotho following months of pressure after he was named as a suspect in the murder of his ex-wife.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lesotho&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Lesotho" title="Politics of Lesotho">Politics of Lesotho</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The Lesotho Government is a parliamentary or <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_monarchy" title="Constitutional monarchy">constitutional monarchy</a>. The Prime Minister, <a href="/wiki/Moeketsi_Majoro" title="Moeketsi Majoro">Moeketsi Majoro</a>, is the <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">head of government</a> and has <a href="/wiki/Executive_authority" class="mw-redirect" title="Executive authority">executive authority</a>. The <a href="/wiki/King_of_Lesotho" class="mw-redirect" title="King of Lesotho">King of Lesotho</a>, <a href="/wiki/Letsie_III_of_Lesotho" class="mw-redirect" title="Letsie III of Lesotho">Letsie III</a>, serves a largely ceremonial function; he no longer possesses any executive authority and is prohibited from actively participating in political initiatives. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/All_Basotho_Convention" title="All Basotho Convention">All Basotho Convention</a> (ABC) leads a <a href="/wiki/Coalition_government" title="Coalition government">coalition government</a> in the <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_of_Lesotho" class="mw-redirect" title="National Assembly of Lesotho">National Assembly</a>, the lower house of parliament. </p>
      <p>The upper house of parliament, called the <a href="/wiki/Senate_of_Lesotho" class="mw-redirect" title="Senate of Lesotho">Senate</a>, is composed of 22 principal chiefs whose membership is hereditary, and 11 appointees of the king, acting on the advice of the prime minister. </p>
      <p>The constitution provides for an independent judicial system, made up of the High Court, the Court of Appeal, Magistrate's Courts, and traditional courts that exist predominantly in rural areas. All but one of the Justices on the Court of Appeal are South African jurists. There is no trial by jury; rather, judges make rulings alone or, in the case of criminal trials, with two other judges as observers. </p>
      <p>The constitution also protects basic <a href="/wiki/Civil_liberties" title="Civil liberties">civil liberties</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_speech" title="Freedom of speech">freedom of speech</a>, <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_association" title="Freedom of association">freedom of association</a>, <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_the_press" title="Freedom of the press">freedom of the press</a>, <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_assembly" title="Freedom of assembly">freedom of peaceful assembly</a> and <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_religion" title="Freedom of religion">freedom of religion</a>. Lesotho was ranked 12th out of 48 sub-Saharan African countries in the 2008 <a href="/wiki/Ibrahim_Index_of_African_Governance" title="Ibrahim Index of African Governance">Ibrahim Index of African Governance</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>As of 2010<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Lesotho&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> the <i><a href="/wiki/People%27s_Charter_Movement" title="People's Charter Movement">People's Charter Movement</a></i> called for the practical annexation of the country by South Africa due to the <a href="/wiki/HIV" title="HIV">HIV</a> epidemic. Nearly a quarter of the population tests positive for <a href="/wiki/HIV" title="HIV">HIV</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> The country has also faced high unemployment, economic collapse, a weak currency and poor travel documents restricting movement. An African Union report called for economic integration of Lesotho with South Africa but stopped short of suggesting annexation. In May 2010 the Charter Movement delivered a petition to the South African <a href="/wiki/High_Commissioner_(Commonwealth)" class="mw-redirect" title="High Commissioner (Commonwealth)">High Commission</a> requesting integration. South Africa's home affairs spokesman Ronnie Mamoepa rejected the idea that Lesotho should be treated as a special case. "It is a sovereign country like South Africa. We sent envoys to our neighbours – Botswana, Zimbabwe, Swaziland and Lesotho – before we enforced the passport rule. When you travel from Britain to South Africa, don't you expect to use a passport?"<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lesotho&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Foreign relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Lesotho" title="Foreign relations of Lesotho">Foreign relations of Lesotho</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:LesothoEmbassyWashingtonDC.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/LesothoEmbassyWashingtonDC.jpg/220px-LesothoEmbassyWashingtonDC.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="176" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/LesothoEmbassyWashingtonDC.jpg/330px-LesothoEmbassyWashingtonDC.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/LesothoEmbassyWashingtonDC.jpg/440px-LesothoEmbassyWashingtonDC.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3565" data-file-height="2857"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:LesothoEmbassyWashingtonDC.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Embassy_of_Lesotho_in_Washington,_D.C." title="Embassy of Lesotho in Washington, D.C.">Embassy</a> in Washington, D.C., United States
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Lesotho's geographic location makes it extremely vulnerable to political and economic developments in South Africa. It is a member of many regional economic organisations, including the <a href="/wiki/Southern_African_Development_Community" title="Southern African Development Community">Southern African Development Community</a> (SADC),<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Southern_African_Customs_Union" title="Southern African Customs Union">Southern African Customs Union</a> (SACU).<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> It is also active in the United Nations (UN), the <a href="/wiki/African_Union" title="African Union">African Union</a> (AU), the <a href="/wiki/Non-Aligned_Movement" title="Non-Aligned Movement">Non-Aligned Movement</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth</a>, and many other international organisations.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Prince" title="Prince">Prince</a> Seeiso Simoné Seeiso is the present High Commissioner of the Kingdom of Lesotho to the <a href="/wiki/Court_of_St._James%27s" class="mw-redirect" title="Court of St. James's">Court of St. James's</a>. The UN is represented by a resident mission as well, including <a href="/wiki/UNDP" class="mw-redirect" title="UNDP">UNDP</a>, <a href="/wiki/UNICEF" title="UNICEF">UNICEF</a>, <a href="/wiki/WHO" class="mw-redirect" title="WHO">WHO</a>, <a href="/wiki/FAO" class="mw-redirect" title="FAO">FAO</a>, <a href="/wiki/WFP" class="mw-redirect" title="WFP">WFP</a>, <a href="/wiki/UNFPA" class="mw-redirect" title="UNFPA">UNFPA</a>, and <a href="/wiki/UNAIDS" class="mw-redirect" title="UNAIDS">UNAIDS</a>. </p>
      <p>Lesotho also has maintained ties with the United Kingdom (Wales in particular), Germany, the United States and other Western states. Although in 1990 it broke relations with the People's Republic of China (PRC) and re-established relations with the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="Republic of China">Republic of China</a> (Taiwan), it later restored ties with the PRC. </p>
      <p>Lesotho also recognises the <a href="/wiki/State_of_Palestine" title="State of Palestine">State of Palestine</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-State_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-State-24">[24]</a></sup> From 2014 up until 2018 Lesotho also recognized the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Kosovo" class="mw-redirect" title="Republic of Kosovo">Republic of Kosovo</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the past, it was a strong public opponent of <a href="/wiki/Apartheid" title="Apartheid">apartheid</a> in South Africa and granted a number of South African refugees political asylum during the apartheid era.<sup id="cite_ref-State_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-State-24">[24]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2019, Lesotho signed the UN <a href="/wiki/Treaty_on_the_Prohibition_of_Nuclear_Weapons" title="Treaty on the Prohibition of Nuclear Weapons">treaty on the Prohibition of Nuclear Weapons</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Law">Law</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lesotho&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Law">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Lesotho does not have a single code containing its laws; it draws them from a variety of sources including: Constitution, Legislation, Common Law, Judicial precedent, Customary Law, and Authoritative texts.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Chinese_Lesotho_project_Lesotho_Parliament_II.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Chinese_Lesotho_project_Lesotho_Parliament_II.jpg/220px-Chinese_Lesotho_project_Lesotho_Parliament_II.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Chinese_Lesotho_project_Lesotho_Parliament_II.jpg/330px-Chinese_Lesotho_project_Lesotho_Parliament_II.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Chinese_Lesotho_project_Lesotho_Parliament_II.jpg/440px-Chinese_Lesotho_project_Lesotho_Parliament_II.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5116" data-file-height="3410"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Chinese_Lesotho_project_Lesotho_Parliament_II.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The Parliament building in Maseru
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Constitution of Lesotho came into force after the publication of the Commencement Order. Constitutionally, legislation refers to laws that have been passed by both houses of parliament and have been assented to by the king (section 78(1)). Subordinate legislation refers to laws passed by other bodies to which parliament has by virtue of section 70(2) of the Constitution validly delegated such legislative powers. These include government publications, ministerial orders, ministerial regulations and municipal <a href="/wiki/By-laws" class="mw-redirect" title="By-laws">by-laws</a>. </p>
      <p>Although Lesotho shares with <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Botswana" title="Botswana">Botswana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Swaziland" class="mw-redirect" title="Swaziland">Swaziland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Namibia" title="Namibia">Namibia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Zimbabwe" title="Zimbabwe">Zimbabwe</a> a mixed general legal system which resulted from the interaction between the Roman-Dutch Civilian law and the <a href="/wiki/English_Common_Law" class="mw-redirect" title="English Common Law">English Common Law</a>, its general law operates independently. Lesotho also applies the common law, which refers to unwritten law or law from non-statutory sources, but excludes customary law. Decisions from South African courts are only persuasive, and courts refer to them in formulating their decisions. Decisions from similar jurisdictions can also be cited for their persuasive value. Magistrates' courts decisions do not become precedent since these are lower courts. They are, however, bound by decisions of the High Court and the Court of Appeal. The most powerful court in the Lesotho justice system is the Court of Appeal, which is the final appellate forum on all matters. It has a supervisory and review jurisdiction over all the courts of Lesotho. </p>
      <p>Lesotho has a dual legal system consisting of customary and general laws operating side by side. Customary law is made up of the customs of the Basotho, written and codified in the Laws of <b>Lerotholi.</b> The general law on the other hand consists of <a href="/wiki/Roman-Dutch_law" title="Roman-Dutch law">Roman Dutch Law</a> imported from the Cape and the Lesotho statutes. The codification of customary law came about after a council was appointed in 1903 to advise the British Resident Commissioner on which laws would be best for governing the <a href="/wiki/Basotho" class="mw-redirect" title="Basotho">Basotho</a>. Until this time, the Basotho customs and laws were passed down from generation to generation through oral tradition. The council was given the task of codifying them, and they came up with the Laws of Lerotholi which are applied by customary courts today (local courts). Written works of eminent authors have persuasive value in the courts of Lesotho. These include writings of the old authorities as well as contemporary writers from similar jurisdictions. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Districts">Districts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lesotho&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Districts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Map_of_lesotho.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Map_of_lesotho.png/220px-Map_of_lesotho.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="193" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Map_of_lesotho.png/330px-Map_of_lesotho.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Map_of_lesotho.png/440px-Map_of_lesotho.png 2x" data-file-width="2464" data-file-height="2159"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Map_of_lesotho.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Districts and Cities of Lesotho
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Lesotho" title="Districts of Lesotho">Districts of Lesotho</a>
      </div> 
      <p>For administrative purposes, Lesotho is divided into <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Lesotho" title="Districts of Lesotho">ten districts</a>, each headed by a district administrator. Each district has a capital known as a <i><a href="/wiki/Camptown_(Lesotho)" class="mw-redirect" title="Camptown (Lesotho)">camptown</a></i>. </p> 
      <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r998391716">.mw-parser-output .div-col{margin-top:0.3em;column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output .div-col-small{font-size:90%}.mw-parser-output .div-col-rules{column-rule:1px solid #aaa}.mw-parser-output .div-col dl,.mw-parser-output .div-col ol,.mw-parser-output .div-col ul{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .div-col li,.mw-parser-output .div-col dd{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}</style>
      <div class="div-col" style="column-width: 30em;"> 
       <ul>
        <li><a href="/wiki/Berea_District" title="Berea District">Berea</a></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Butha-Buthe_District" title="Butha-Buthe District">Butha-Buthe</a></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Leribe_District" title="Leribe District">Leribe</a></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Mafeteng_District" title="Mafeteng District">Mafeteng</a></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Maseru_District" title="Maseru District">Maseru</a></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Mohale%27s_Hoek_District" title="Mohale's Hoek District">Mohale's Hoek</a></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Mokhotlong_District" title="Mokhotlong District">Mokhotlong</a></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Qacha%27s_Nek_District" title="Qacha's Nek District">Qacha's Nek</a></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Quthing_District" title="Quthing District">Quthing</a></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Thaba-Tseka_District" title="Thaba-Tseka District">Thaba-Tseka</a></li>
       </ul>
      </div> 
      <p>The districts are subdivided into 80 constituencies, which consist of 129 local <a href="/wiki/Community_councils_of_Lesotho" title="Community councils of Lesotho">community councils</a>. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lesotho&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Lesotho" title="Geography of Lesotho">Geography of Lesotho</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:AfriSki.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/AfriSki.jpg/220px-AfriSki.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/AfriSki.jpg/330px-AfriSki.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/AfriSki.jpg/440px-AfriSki.jpg 2x" data-file-width="624" data-file-height="416"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:AfriSki.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Afriski" title="Afriski">Afriski</a> resort in the <a href="/wiki/Maloti_Mountains" title="Maloti Mountains">Maloti Mountains</a> of Lesotho
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Lesotho covers 30,355&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (11,720&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi). It is the only independent state in the world that lies entirely above 1,000 metres (3,281&nbsp;ft) in elevation. Its lowest point of 1,400 metres (4,593&nbsp;ft) is thus the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_lowest_point" class="mw-redirect" title="List of countries by lowest point">highest lowest point of any country in the world</a>. Over 80 percent of the country lies above 1,800 metres (5,906&nbsp;ft). Lesotho is also the southernmost landlocked country in the world and is entirely surrounded by South Africa. It lies between latitudes <a href="/wiki/28th_parallel_south" title="28th parallel south">28°</a> and <a href="/wiki/31st_parallel_south" title="31st parallel south">31°S</a>, and longitudes <a href="/wiki/27th_meridian_east" title="27th meridian east">27°</a> and <a href="/wiki/30th_meridian_east" title="30th meridian east">30°E</a>. About 12% of Lesotho is arable land, however, this land is vulnerable to <a href="/wiki/Soil_erosion" title="Soil erosion">soil erosion</a>, and it is estimated that 40 million tons of soil are lost each year due to erosion.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-28">[28]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lesotho&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_Lesotho" class="mw-redirect" title="Climate of Lesotho">Climate of Lesotho</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Because of its elevation, Lesotho remains cooler throughout the year than other regions at the same latitude. Most of the rain falls as summer <a href="/wiki/Thunderstorm" title="Thunderstorm">thunderstorms</a>. <a href="/wiki/Maseru" title="Maseru">Maseru</a> and surrounding lowlands often reach 30&nbsp;°C (86&nbsp;°F) in summer. Winters can be cold with the lowlands getting down to −7&nbsp;°C (19&nbsp;°F) and the highlands to −18&nbsp;°C (0&nbsp;°F) at times. Snow is common in the highlands between May and September; the higher peaks can experience snowfalls year-round. Rainfall in Lesotho is highly variable regarding both when and where precipitation occurs. Despite Lesotho's small size, annual precipitation can vary from 500mm annual in one area to 1200mm in another because of elevation.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-28">[28]</a></sup> The summer season that stretches from October to April sees the most rainfall, and from December to February, the majority of the country receives over 100mm of rain a month.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_28-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-28">[28]</a></sup> The least monthly rainfall in Lesotho occurs in June when most regions receive less than 15mm a month.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_28-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-28">[28]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Drought">Drought</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lesotho&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Drought">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Early_Morning_view_from_Sehlabathebe_House_-_panoramio.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Early_Morning_view_from_Sehlabathebe_House_-_panoramio.jpg/220px-Early_Morning_view_from_Sehlabathebe_House_-_panoramio.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Early_Morning_view_from_Sehlabathebe_House_-_panoramio.jpg/330px-Early_Morning_view_from_Sehlabathebe_House_-_panoramio.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Early_Morning_view_from_Sehlabathebe_House_-_panoramio.jpg/440px-Early_Morning_view_from_Sehlabathebe_House_-_panoramio.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Early_Morning_view_from_Sehlabathebe_House_-_panoramio.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Hills in Lesoto
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Periodic <a href="/wiki/Drought" title="Drought">droughts</a> have a serious effect on Lesotho's majority rural population as many people living outside of urban areas rely on subsistence farming or small scale agriculture as their primary source of income.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-29">[29]</a></sup> Droughts in Lesotho are exacerbated by poor agricultural practices.<sup id="cite_ref-:3_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-30">[30]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/The_World_Factbook" title="The World Factbook">The World Fact Book</a> lists periodic droughts under the 'Natural Hazard' section of Lesotho's section of the publication.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2007, Lesotho experienced its worst drought in 30 years and was advised by the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> to declare a state of emergency to get aid from international organizations.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-29">[29]</a></sup> Erratic weather and the corresponding decline of the humanitarian situation still present Lesotho with problems currently. <a href="/wiki/Famine_Early_Warning_Systems_Network" title="Famine Early Warning Systems Network">The Famine Early Warning System Network</a> most recently reported that the rainy season of 2018/2019 not only started a month later than normal but also has recorded below-average amounts of rain.<sup id="cite_ref-:4_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-32">[32]</a></sup> Also, data from the Climate Hazards Group InfraRed Precipitation Station (CHIRP) shows rainfall in Lesotho between October 2018 and February 2019 ranged from 55% to 80% below normal rates.<sup id="cite_ref-:4_32-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-32">[32]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In March 2019, the Lesotho Vulnerability Assessment and Analysis Committee conducted a report that initially predicted that 487,857 people in the country need humanitarian assistance because of the effects of drought.<sup id="cite_ref-:4_32-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-32">[32]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>There are a variety of different ways drought in Lesotho has led to the need for humanitarian assistance. Poor hygiene practices that result from a lack of clean water can cause cases of <a href="/wiki/Typhoid_fever" title="Typhoid fever">typhoid</a> and <a href="/wiki/Diarrhea" title="Diarrhea">diarrhea</a>. Lack of available water also indirectly leads to an increased risk for women and girls who collect water for household consumption as they must spend more time and travel long distances while running the risk of being physically or sexually assaulted.<sup id="cite_ref-:4_32-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-32">[32]</a></sup> Drought in Lesotho also leads to both migration to more urban areas and immigration to South Africa for new opportunities and to escape food insecurity.<sup id="cite_ref-:3_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-30">[30]</a></sup> The report also found that between July 2019 and June 2020 640,000 people in Lesotho are expected to be affected by food insecurity as a result of unproductive harvests as well as the corresponding rise in <a href="/wiki/Food_prices" title="Food prices">food prices</a> because of the drought.<sup id="cite_ref-:4_32-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-32">[32]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Wildlife">Wildlife</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lesotho&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Wildlife">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Aloe_polyphylla_3.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Aloe_polyphylla_3.jpg/220px-Aloe_polyphylla_3.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Aloe_polyphylla_3.jpg/330px-Aloe_polyphylla_3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Aloe_polyphylla_3.jpg/440px-Aloe_polyphylla_3.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1800" data-file-height="2400"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Aloe_polyphylla_3.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><i><a href="/wiki/Aloe_polyphylla" title="Aloe polyphylla">Aloe polyphylla</a></i>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_of_Lesotho" title="Wildlife of Lesotho">Wildlife of Lesotho</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Category:Environment_of_Lesotho" title="Category:Environment of Lesotho">Category:Environment of Lesotho</a>
      </div>
      <p>There are known to be <a href="/wiki/List_of_birds_of_Lesotho" title="List of birds of Lesotho">339 bird species</a> in Lesotho, including 10 globally threatened species and 2 introduced species, <a href="/wiki/List_of_reptiles_of_Lesotho" title="List of reptiles of Lesotho">17 reptile species</a>, including geckos, snakes and lizards, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_mammals_of_Lesotho" title="List of mammals of Lesotho">60 mammal species</a> endemic to Lesotho, including the endangered <a href="/wiki/White-tailed_rat" title="White-tailed rat">white-tailed rat</a>. </p>
      <p>Lesotho's flora is <a href="/wiki/Alpine_plants" class="mw-redirect" title="Alpine plants">Alpine</a>, due to the high and mountainous terrain. The <a href="/wiki/Katse_Botanical_Gardens" title="Katse Botanical Gardens">Katse Botanical Gardens</a> houses a collection of <a href="/wiki/Medicinal_plants" title="Medicinal plants">medicinal plants</a> and has a large seed bank of plants from the <a href="/wiki/Malibamat%27so_River" title="Malibamat'so River">Malibamat'so River</a> area.<sup id="cite_ref-golesotho_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-golesotho-33">[33]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> Three terrestrial ecoregions lie within Lesotho's boundaries: <a href="/wiki/Drakensberg_alti-montane_grasslands_and_woodlands" class="mw-redirect" title="Drakensberg alti-montane grasslands and woodlands">Drakensberg alti-montane grasslands and woodlands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Drakensberg_montane_grasslands" class="mw-redirect" title="Drakensberg montane grasslands">Drakensberg montane grasslands</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Highveld_grasslands" class="mw-redirect" title="Highveld grasslands">Highveld grasslands</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DinersteinOlson2017_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DinersteinOlson2017-35">[35]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lesotho&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Lesotho" title="Economy of Lesotho">Economy of Lesotho</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:A_vehicle_on_Sani_Pass.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/A_vehicle_on_Sani_Pass.jpg/220px-A_vehicle_on_Sani_Pass.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/A_vehicle_on_Sani_Pass.jpg/330px-A_vehicle_on_Sani_Pass.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/A_vehicle_on_Sani_Pass.jpg/440px-A_vehicle_on_Sani_Pass.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1063"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:A_vehicle_on_Sani_Pass.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Sani_Pass" title="Sani Pass">Sani Pass</a> on the border is a popular tourist attraction.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Lesotho is geographically surrounded by South Africa and economically integrated with it. The economy of Lesotho is based on agriculture, livestock, manufacturing and mining, and depends heavily on inflows of workers' <a href="/wiki/Remittance" title="Remittance">remittances</a> and receipts from the Southern African Customs Union (SACU).<sup id="cite_ref-worldbank_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-worldbank-36">[36]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> The majority of households subsist on farming. The formal sector employment consists mainly of female workers in the apparel sector, male migrant labour, primarily miners in South Africa for three to nine months, and employment by the Government of Lesotho (GOL). The western lowlands form the main agricultural zone. Almost 50 percent of the population earn income through informal crop cultivation or animal husbandry with nearly two-thirds of the country's income coming from the agricultural sector. The percentage of the population living below USD <a href="/wiki/Purchasing_Power_Parity" class="mw-redirect" title="Purchasing Power Parity">Purchasing Power Parity</a> (PPP) US$1.25/day fell from 48 percent to 44 percent between 1995 and 2003.<sup id="cite_ref-worldbank_36-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-worldbank-36">[36]</a></sup> The country is among the "Low Human Development" countries (rank 160 of 187 on the <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a> as classified by the UNDP, with 52 years of life expectancy at birth.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:0_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-39">[39]</a></sup> Adult literacy is as high as 82 percent. Among the children below the age of five years, 20 percent are under weight.<sup id="cite_ref-undp_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-undp-40">[40]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Lesotho has taken advantage of the <a href="/wiki/African_Growth_and_Opportunity_Act" title="African Growth and Opportunity Act">African Growth and Opportunity Act</a> (AGOA) to become the largest exporter of garments to the US from sub-Saharan Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> US brands and retailers sourcing from Lesotho include: Foot Locker, Gap, Gloria Vanderbilt, JCPenney, Levi Strauss, Saks, Sears, Timberland and Wal-Mart.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> In mid-2004 its employment reached over 50,000, mainly female workers, marking the first time that manufacturing sector workers outnumbered government employees. In 2008 it exported goods worth 487 million dollars mainly to the US. Since 2004, employment in the sector has dwindled to about 45,000 in mid-2011 due to international competition in the garment sector. It was the largest formal sector employer in Lesotho in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-smartlessons.ifc.org_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-smartlessons.ifc.org-43">[43]</a></sup> In 2007, the average earnings of an employee in the textile sector were US$103 per month, and the official minimum wage for a general textile worker was US$93 per month. The average gross national income per capita in 2008 was US$83 per month.<sup id="cite_ref-smartlessons.ifc.org_43-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-smartlessons.ifc.org-43">[43]</a></sup> The sector initiated a major program to fight HIV/AIDS called Apparel Lesotho Alliance to Fight AIDS (ALAFA). It is an industry-wide program providing disease prevention and treatment for workers.<sup id="cite_ref-alafa_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-alafa-44">[44]</a></sup> </p> 
      <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r978413945/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{display:flex;flex-direction:column}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{display:flex;flex-direction:row;clear:left;flex-wrap:wrap;width:100%;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{margin:1px;float:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .theader{clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;align-self:center;background-color:transparent;width:100%}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-left{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-right{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-center{text-align:center}@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;max-width:none!important;align-items:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{justify-content:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle .thumbcaption{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow>.thumbcaption{text-align:center}}</style>
      <div class="thumb tmulti tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:312px;max-width:312px">
        <div class="trow">
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:182px;max-width:182px">
          <div class="thumbimage" style="height:123px;overflow:hidden">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Katse_Dam-001.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Katse_Dam-001.jpg/180px-Katse_Dam-001.jpg" decoding="async" width="180" height="120" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Katse_Dam-001.jpg/270px-Katse_Dam-001.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Katse_Dam-001.jpg/360px-Katse_Dam-001.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3008" data-file-height="2000"></a>
          </div>
          <div class="thumbcaption text-align-center">
           <a href="/wiki/Katse_Dam" title="Katse Dam">Katse Dam</a>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:126px;max-width:126px">
          <div class="thumbimage" style="height:123px;overflow:hidden">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Mohale_Dam_2008.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Mohale_Dam_2008.jpg/124px-Mohale_Dam_2008.jpg" decoding="async" width="124" height="165" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Mohale_Dam_2008.jpg/186px-Mohale_Dam_2008.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Mohale_Dam_2008.jpg/248px-Mohale_Dam_2008.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2448" data-file-height="3264"></a>
          </div>
          <div class="thumbcaption text-align-center">
           <a href="/wiki/Mohale_Dam" title="Mohale Dam">Mohale Dam</a>
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Water and <a href="/wiki/Diamonds" class="mw-redirect" title="Diamonds">diamonds</a> are Lesotho's significant natural resources.<sup id="cite_ref-worldbank_36-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-worldbank-36">[36]</a></sup> Water is used through the 21-year, multibillion-dollar <a href="/wiki/Lesotho_Highlands_Water_Project" title="Lesotho Highlands Water Project">Lesotho Highlands Water Project</a> (LHWP), under the authority of the Lesotho Highlands Development Authority. The project commenced in 1986.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> The LHWP is designed to capture, store, and transfer water from the <a href="/wiki/Orange_River" title="Orange River">Orange River</a> system to South Africa's Free State and greater Johannesburg area, which features a large concentration of South African industry, population, and agriculture. Completion of the first phase of the project has made Lesotho almost completely self-sufficient in the production of electricity and generated approximately US$70 million in 2010 from the sale of electricity and water to South Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a>, <a href="/wiki/African_Development_Bank" title="African Development Bank">African Development Bank</a>, <a href="/wiki/European_Investment_Bank" title="European Investment Bank">European Investment Bank</a>, and many other bilateral donors financed the project. </p>
      <p>Diamonds are produced at the Letšeng, Mothae, Liqhobong, and Kao mines, which combined are estimated to produce 240,000 carats of diamonds in 2014, worth US$300 million. The Letšeng mine is estimated to produce diamonds with an average value of US$2172/carat, making it the world's richest mine on an average price per carat basis.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> The sector suffered a setback in 2008 as the result of the world recession, but rebounded in 2010 and 2011. Export of diamonds reached US$230 million in 2010–2011.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> In 1957, a South African adventurer, colonel Jack Scott, accompanied by a young man named Keith Whitelock, set out prospecting for diamonds. They found their diamond mine at 3,100 m elevation, on top of the Maluti Mountains in northeastern Lesotho, some 70&nbsp;km from Mokhotlong at Letšeng. In 1967, a 601-carat (120.2&nbsp;g) diamond (Lesotho Brown) was discovered in the mountains by a Mosotho woman. In August 2006, a 603-carat (120.6&nbsp;g) white diamond, the <a href="/wiki/Lesotho_Promise" title="Lesotho Promise">Lesotho Promise</a>, was discovered at the Letšeng-la-Terae mine. Another 478-carat (95.6&nbsp;g) diamond was discovered at the same location in 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Lesotho has progressed in moving from a predominantly subsistence-oriented economy to a lower middle income economy exporting natural resources and manufacturing goods. The exporting sectors have brought higher and more secure incomes to a significant portion of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-worldbank_36-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-worldbank-36">[36]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>However, the global economic crisis hit the Lesotho economy hard. Lesotho suffered a loss of textile exports and jobs in this sector due largely to the economic slowdown in the United States, one of their major export destinations. Reduced diamond mining and exports, including a drop in the price of diamonds as well as a drop in SACU revenues due to the economic slowdown in the South African economy also contributed to the crisis. Finally reduction in worker remittances due to weakening of the South African economy and contraction of the mining sector and related job losses in South Africa contributed to in 2009, Lesotho's GDP growth slowing to 0.9 percent.<sup id="cite_ref-worldbank_36-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-worldbank-36">[36]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The official currency is the <a href="/wiki/Lesotho_loti" title="Lesotho loti">loti</a> (plural: maloti), but can be used interchangeably with the <a href="/wiki/South_African_rand" title="South African rand">South African rand</a>. Lesotho, Eswatini, Namibia, and South Africa also form a common currency and exchange control area known as the <a href="/wiki/Common_Monetary_Area" title="Common Monetary Area">Common Monetary Area</a> (CMA). The loti is at par with the rand. One hundred <i>lisente</i> (singular: <i>sente</i>) equal one loti. </p>
      <p>Lesotho is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Southern_African_Customs_Union" title="Southern African Customs Union">Southern African Customs Union</a> (SACU), in which tariffs have been eliminated on the trade of goods between other member countries <a href="/wiki/Botswana" title="Botswana">Botswana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Namibia" title="Namibia">Namibia</a>, South Africa, and <a href="/wiki/Eswatini" title="Eswatini">Eswatini</a>. Lesotho has received economic aid from a variety of sources, including the United States, the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a>, Republic of Ireland, the United Kingdom, the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>, and Germany. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lesotho&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Lesotho" title="Demographics of Lesotho">Demographics of Lesotho</a>
      </div>
