      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics_2">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lesotho&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Lesotho has a population of approximately 2,108,328<sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP-2">[2]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_2019_3-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP_2019-3">[3]</a></sup>. The population distribution of Lesotho is 25 percent urban and 75 percent rural. However, it is estimated that the annual increase in urban population is 3.5 percent.<sup id="cite_ref-factbook_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factbook-50">[50]</a></sup> Population density is lower in the highlands than in the western lowlands. Although the majority of the population—60.2 percent—is between 15 and 64 years of age, Lesotho has a substantial youth population numbering around 34.8 percent.<sup id="cite_ref-factbook_50-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factbook-50">[50]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnic_groups_and_languages">Ethnic groups and languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lesotho&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Ethnic groups and languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Lesotho's ethno-linguistic structure consists almost entirely of the <a href="/wiki/Basotho" class="mw-redirect" title="Basotho">Basotho</a>, a Bantu-speaking people: an estimated 99.7 percent of the people identify as Basotho. In this regard, Lesotho is part of a handful of <a href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_Africa" title="Sub-Saharan Africa">sub-Saharan African</a> countries that are <a href="/wiki/Nation_states" class="mw-redirect" title="Nation states">nation states</a> with a single dominant cultural ethnic group and language; majority of sub-Saharan African nations' borders were drawn by <a href="/wiki/Colonisation_of_Africa" title="Colonisation of Africa">colonial powers</a> and do not correspond to ethnic boundaries or pre-colonial polities.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBoyd19791_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBoyd19791-51">[51]</a></sup> Basotho subgroups include the Bafokeng (<i>totems: <b>phoka</b> (dew), '<b>mutla</b> (hare)</i>), Batloung (<i>totem: <b>tlou</b> (elephant)</i>), Baphuthi (<i>totem: <b>phuthi</b></i>), Bakuena (<i>totem: <b>kuena</b> (crocodile)</i>), Bataung (<i>totem: <b>tau</b> (lion)</i>), Batšoeneng (<i>totem: <b>tšoene</b></i>), and <a href="/wiki/Matebele" class="mw-redirect" title="Matebele">Matebele</a>. </p>
      <p>The main language, <a href="/wiki/Sesotho" class="mw-redirect" title="Sesotho">Sesotho</a>, is also the first official and administrative language, and it is what Basotho speak on an ordinary basis. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lesotho&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:St_Michaels_Cathedral,_lesotho.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/St_Michaels_Cathedral%2C_lesotho.jpg/220px-St_Michaels_Cathedral%2C_lesotho.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/St_Michaels_Cathedral%2C_lesotho.jpg/330px-St_Michaels_Cathedral%2C_lesotho.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/St_Michaels_Cathedral%2C_lesotho.jpg/440px-St_Michaels_Cathedral%2C_lesotho.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4922" data-file-height="3281"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:St_Michaels_Cathedral,_lesotho.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>St.Michaels Cathedral
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Lesotho" title="Religion in Lesotho">Religion in Lesotho</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The population of Lesotho is estimated to be more than 95% Christian.<sup id="cite_ref-Pew_Christians_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pew_Christians-52">[52]</a></sup> Protestants account for 50% of the population, (<a href="/wiki/Evangelicalism" title="Evangelicalism">Evangelicals</a> 17.5%, <a href="/wiki/Anglican_Communion" title="Anglican Communion">Anglicans</a> 7.5%, <a href="/wiki/Pentecostalism" title="Pentecostalism">Pentecostals</a> 21.9% and other Christians an additional 8.5%).<sup id="cite_ref-DHS_2014_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DHS_2014-53">[53]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholics</a> represent nearly 40 percent of the population, served by the province of the Metropolitan <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Archdiocese_of_Maseru" title="Roman Catholic Archdiocese of Maseru">Archbishop of Maseru</a> and his three suffragans (the bishops of <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_Leribe" title="Roman Catholic Diocese of Leribe">Leribe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_Mohale%27s_Hoek" title="Roman Catholic Diocese of Mohale's Hoek">Mohale's Hoek</a> and <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_Qacha%27s_Nek" title="Roman Catholic Diocese of Qacha's Nek">Qacha's Nek</a>), who also form the national <a href="/wiki/Episcopal_conference" title="Episcopal conference">episcopal conference</a>. Non-Christian religions represent only 1.5% of the population, and those of no religion 3.5%.<sup id="cite_ref-DHS_2014_53-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DHS_2014-53">[53]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education_and_literacy">Education and literacy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lesotho&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Education and literacy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:National_University_of_Lesotho_Administration_Block.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/National_University_of_Lesotho_Administration_Block.jpg/220px-National_University_of_Lesotho_Administration_Block.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/National_University_of_Lesotho_Administration_Block.jpg/330px-National_University_of_Lesotho_Administration_Block.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/National_University_of_Lesotho_Administration_Block.jpg/440px-National_University_of_Lesotho_Administration_Block.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2174" data-file-height="1449"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:National_University_of_Lesotho_Administration_Block.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/National_University_of_Lesotho" title="National University of Lesotho">National University of Lesotho</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>According to recent estimates, 85% of women and 68% of men over the age of 15 are literate.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> As such, Lesotho holds one of the highest literacy rates in Africa,<sup id="cite_ref-factbook_50-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factbook-50">[50]</a></sup> in part because Lesotho invests over 12% of its GDP in education.<sup id="cite_ref-unesco_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unesco-55">[55]</a></sup> Unlike in most other countries, in Lesotho female literacy (84.93%) exceeds male literacy (67.75%) by 17.18%. According to a study by the Southern and Eastern Africa Consortium for Monitoring Educational Quality in 2000, 37 percent of grade six pupils in Lesotho (average age 14 years) are at or above reading level four, "Reading for Meaning."<sup id="cite_ref-sacmeq_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sacmeq-56">[56]</a></sup> A pupil at this level of literacy can read ahead or backwards through various parts of text to link and interpret information. Although education is not compulsory, the Government of Lesotho is incrementally implementing a program for free primary education.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Despite their literacy, Lesotho's residents struggle for access to vital services, such as healthcare, travel and educational resources, as, according to the <a href="/wiki/International_Telecommunication_Union" title="International Telecommunication Union">International Telecommunication Union</a>, only 3.4% of the population use the Internet. A service from <a href="/wiki/Telecom_Lesotho" class="mw-redirect" title="Telecom Lesotho">Econet Telecom Lesotho</a> expanded the country's access to email through entry-level, low-end mobile phones and, consequently, improved access to educational information. The <a href="/wiki/African_Library_Project" title="African Library Project">African Library Project</a> works to establish school and village libraries in partnership with US Peace Corps Lesotho<sup id="cite_ref-peacecorps_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-peacecorps-58">[58]</a></sup> and the Butha Buthe District of Education. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lesotho&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Health_in_Lesotho" title="Health in Lesotho">Health in Lesotho</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Life expectancy at birth in Lesotho in 2016 was 51 years for men and 55 for women. Infant mortality is about 8.3%. In 2019, life expectancy was estimated at 52 years for men and women.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_39-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-39">[39]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>As of 2018, Lesotho's adult <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_HIV/AIDS_adult_prevalence_rate" title="List of countries by HIV/AIDS adult prevalence rate">HIV/AIDS prevalence rate</a> of 23.6% was the second highest in the world, after <a href="/wiki/Eswatini" title="Eswatini">Eswatini</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The country has the highest incidence of <a href="/wiki/Tuberculosis" title="Tuberculosis">tuberculosis</a> in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Security">Security</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lesotho&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Security">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Lesotho_Defence_Force_Deputy_Commander_Maj._Gen._Motsomotso_Medical_Readiness_Excercise_14-1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Lesotho_Defence_Force_Deputy_Commander_Maj._Gen._Motsomotso_Medical_Readiness_Excercise_14-1.jpg/220px-Lesotho_Defence_Force_Deputy_Commander_Maj._Gen._Motsomotso_Medical_Readiness_Excercise_14-1.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="193" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Lesotho_Defence_Force_Deputy_Commander_Maj._Gen._Motsomotso_Medical_Readiness_Excercise_14-1.jpg/330px-Lesotho_Defence_Force_Deputy_Commander_Maj._Gen._Motsomotso_Medical_Readiness_Excercise_14-1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Lesotho_Defence_Force_Deputy_Commander_Maj._Gen._Motsomotso_Medical_Readiness_Excercise_14-1.jpg/440px-Lesotho_Defence_Force_Deputy_Commander_Maj._Gen._Motsomotso_Medical_Readiness_Excercise_14-1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2700" data-file-height="2363"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Lesotho_Defence_Force_Deputy_Commander_Maj._Gen._Motsomotso_Medical_Readiness_Excercise_14-1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>LDF Deputy Commander briefing soldiers
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The internal and external security of Lesotho is the responsibility of the Defence Commission, which is established and defined by article 145 of the Lesotho national Constitution. The Prime Minister is the Chairman <i>ex officio</i>, and there are six other Defence Commission members, namely the Commander and Deputy Commander of the Lesotho Defence Force, the Commissioner and Assistant Commissioner of the Lesotho Mounted Police Service, and the Director and Deputy Director of the Lesotho National Security Service. The Defence Commission has power to strategically direct the defence force, the police, and the prison service, but not the security service, which is answerable only to the Government. The Defence Commission has power to appoint or remove the senior staff of the defence force, police, and prison service, but not the security service, whose Director and Deputy Director are personal appointments of the Prime Minister.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Lesotho_Defence_Force" title="Lesotho Defence Force">Lesotho Defence Force</a> (LDF) is established under article 146 of the national Constitution, and charged with the maintenance of internal security and the defence of Lesotho. Its chief officer is designated <i>Commander</i> by the Constitution,<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> and usually holds the rank of <a href="/wiki/Lieutenant-general" class="mw-redirect" title="Lieutenant-general">lieutenant-general</a>. The LDF has a total strength of just over 3,000. The largest component is infantry, but they are supported by small artillery, logistics, and air force units, and a single <a href="/wiki/Armoured_reconnaissance" title="Armoured reconnaissance">armoured reconnaissance</a> <a href="/wiki/Company_(military_unit)" title="Company (military unit)">company</a>. Since 2000, Lesotho Defence Forces have been trained by a small contingent of Indian Army Training Team, led by a Brigadier.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Lesotho_Mounted_Police_Service" title="Lesotho Mounted Police Service">Lesotho Mounted Police Service</a> (LMPS) is established under article 147 of the national Constitution, and charged with the maintenance of law and order. Its chief officer is designated <i>Commissioner</i> by the Constitution. The LMPS provides uniformed policing, criminal detection, and traffic policing. There are specialist units dealing with high-tech crime, immigration, wildlife, and terrorism. The current force has existed, despite changes of name, continuously since 1872. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/w/index.php?title=Lesotho_National_Security_Service&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Lesotho National Security Service (page does not exist)">Lesotho National Security Service</a> (LNSS) is established under article 148 of the national Constitution, and charged with the protection of national security. Its chief officer is designated <i>Director</i> by the Constitution. The LNSS is an intelligence service, reporting directly to the Government. The power to appoint or dismiss a Director is vested directly in the Prime Minister. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lesotho&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Parade_of_Basotho_women.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Parade_of_Basotho_women.jpg/220px-Parade_of_Basotho_women.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="254" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Parade_of_Basotho_women.jpg/330px-Parade_of_Basotho_women.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Parade_of_Basotho_women.jpg/440px-Parade_of_Basotho_women.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1304" data-file-height="1508"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Parade_of_Basotho_women.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Women wearing <a href="/wiki/Basotho_blanket" title="Basotho blanket">Basotho blankets</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Lesotho" title="Music of Lesotho">Music of Lesotho</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_African_writers_by_country#Lesotho" title="List of African writers by country">List of African writers by country §&nbsp;Lesotho</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Traditional musical instruments include the <i>lekolulo</i>, a kind of flute used by herding boys, the <i>setolo-tolo</i>, played by men using their mouth, and the woman's stringed <i>thomo</i>. </p>
      <p>The national anthem of Lesotho is "<i>Lesotho Fatše La Bo-ntata Rona</i>", which literally translates into "Lesotho, Land of Our Fore-Fathers". </p>
      <p>The traditional style of housing in Lesotho is called a mokhoro. Many older houses, especially in smaller towns and villages, are of this type, with walls usually constructed from large stones cemented together. Baked mud bricks and especially <a href="/wiki/Concrete_masonry_unit" title="Concrete masonry unit">concrete blocks</a> are also used nowadays, with thatched roofs still common, although often replaced by corrugated roofing sheets. </p>
      <p>Traditional attire revolves around the <a href="/wiki/Basotho_blanket" title="Basotho blanket">Basotho blanket</a>, a thick covering made primarily of wool. The blankets are ubiquitous throughout the country during all seasons, and worn differently by men and women. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Morija_Arts_%26_Cultural_Festival" title="Morija Arts &amp; Cultural Festival">Morija Arts &amp; Cultural Festival</a> is a prominent Sesotho arts and music festival. It is held annually in the historical town of Morija, where the first missionaries arrived in 1833. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lesotho&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Cuisine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Cuisine_of_Lesotho" title="Cuisine of Lesotho">cuisine of Lesotho</a> includes African traditions and British influences.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> The national dish of Lesotho is Motoho, a fermented sorghum porridge eaten throughout the country. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Traditional_food">Traditional food</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lesotho&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Traditional food">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>Because Lesotho has limited food resources, a majority of families in the country raise their own food and <a href="/wiki/Livestock" title="Livestock">livestock</a> to support themselves and their families. </p>
      <p>Some staple foods include <a href="/wiki/Pap_(food)" class="mw-redirect" title="Pap (food)">papa</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Cornmeal" title="Cornmeal">cornmeal</a> <a href="/wiki/Porridge" title="Porridge">porridge</a> covered with a sauce consisting of various vegetables. <a href="/wiki/Tea" title="Tea">Tea</a> and locally brewed <a href="/wiki/Beer" title="Beer">beer</a> are popular choices for beverages.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Traditional_costumes">Traditional costumes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lesotho&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Traditional costumes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The traditional clothing in Lesotho is specific depending on the region of the country. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:2008-02-09_Xhosa_women.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/2008-02-09_Xhosa_women.jpg/220px-2008-02-09_Xhosa_women.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/2008-02-09_Xhosa_women.jpg/330px-2008-02-09_Xhosa_women.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/2008-02-09_Xhosa_women.jpg/440px-2008-02-09_Xhosa_women.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2304"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:2008-02-09_Xhosa_women.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Shweshwe clothing
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lesotho&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>2018 film <i><a href="/wiki/Black_Panther_(film)" title="Black Panther (film)">Black Panther</a></i> director <a href="/wiki/Ryan_Coogler" title="Ryan Coogler">Ryan Coogler</a> stated that his depiction of <a href="/wiki/Wakanda" title="Wakanda">Wakanda</a> was inspired by Lesotho.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> Basotho blankets also became more known as a result of the film.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> In November 2020, the film <i><a href="/wiki/This_Is_Not_a_Burial,_It%27s_a_Resurrection" title="This Is Not a Burial, It's a Resurrection">This Is Not a Burial, It's a Resurrection</a></i> became the first Lesotho film to be submitted for the <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_International_Feature_Film" title="Academy Award for Best International Feature Film">Academy Award for Best International Feature Film</a> by the country.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Social_issues">Social issues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lesotho&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Social issues">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>Significant levels of <a href="/wiki/Child_labour" title="Child labour">child labour</a> exist in Lesotho, and the country is in the process of formulating an Action Program on the Elimination of Child Labor (APEC). According to the UN, Lesotho has the highest rape rate of any country (91.6 per 100,000 people rate for reported rape in 2008).<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Treatment of people with <a href="/wiki/Disability" title="Disability">disabilities</a> is another major issue facing the country. According to the Lesotho Census of 2006, around four percent of the population is thought to have some sort of disability. However, there are concerns regarding the reliability of the methodologies used and the real figure is thought to be closer to the global estimate of 15 percent. According to a survey conducted by the Lesotho National Federation of Organisations of the Disabled in conjunction with SINTEF,<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> people with disability in Lesotho face significant social and cultural barriers which prevent them from accessing education, healthcare, and employment on an equal basis with others. </p>
      <p>On 2 December 2008 Lesotho became the 42nd country in the world to sign the UN <a href="/wiki/Convention_on_the_Rights_of_Persons_with_Disabilities" title="Convention on the Rights of Persons with Disabilities">Convention on the Rights of Persons with Disabilities</a>. However, to date the treaty has yet to be domesticated. Despite lobbying efforts from disabled persons organisations, there have been no moves to develop disability specific legislation to protect the <a href="/wiki/Disability_rights" class="mw-redirect" title="Disability rights">rights of people with disabilities</a>. Although the National Disability and Rehabilitation Policy was developed in 2011, thus far there has been no budget allocated for its implementation. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Sexual_violence" title="Sexual violence">Sexual violence</a> in Lesotho is a serious problem. International data from <a href="/wiki/UNODC" class="mw-redirect" title="UNODC">UNODC</a> found the incidence of rapes recorded in 2008 by the police to be the highest in Lesotho.<sup id="cite_ref-unodc1_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unodc1-71">[71]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>One study in Lesotho found that 61 percent of women reported having experienced sexual violence at some point in their lives, of which 22 percent reported being physically forced to have sexual intercourse.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> In the 2009 <a href="/wiki/Demographic_and_Health_Surveys" title="Demographic and Health Surveys">DHS survey</a> 15.7 percent of men said that a husband is justified in hitting or beating his wife if she refuses to have sex with him, while 16 percent said a husband is justified to use force to have sex.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> In another study, researchers have concluded that "Given the high prevalence of HIV in Lesotho, programs should address women's right to control their sexuality."<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <i>Married Persons Equality Act 2006</i> gives equal rights to wives in regard to their husbands, abolishing the husband's <a href="/wiki/Marital_power" title="Marital power">marital power</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The World Economic Forum's 2020 Gender Gap Report ranks Lesotho 88th in the world for gender parity, while neighboring South Africa ranks 17th.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>According to a 2016 study conducted by the World Health Organization, Lesotho also has the highest rate of suicide per capita for females in the entire world.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint noexcerpt Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="This claim needs references to better sources. (February 2021)">better&nbsp;source&nbsp;needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lesotho&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r936637989">.mw-parser-output .portal{border:solid #aaa 1px;padding:0}.mw-parser-output .portal.tleft{margin:0.5em 1em 0.5em 0}.mw-parser-output .portal.tright{margin:0.5em 0 0.5em 1em}.mw-parser-output .portal>ul{display:table;box-sizing:border-box;padding:0.1em;max-width:175px;background:#f9f9f9;font-size:85%;line-height:110%;font-style:italic;font-weight:bold}.mw-parser-output .portal>ul>li{display:table-row}.mw-parser-output .portal>ul>li>span:first-child{display:table-cell;padding:0.2em;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .portal>ul>li>span:last-child{display:table-cell;padding:0.2em 0.2em 0.2em 0.3em;vertical-align:middle}</style>

        <li><span><img alt="map" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Africa_%28orthographic_projection%29.svg/28px-Africa_%28orthographic_projection%29.svg.png" decoding="async" width="28" height="28" class="noviewer" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Africa_%28orthographic_projection%29.svg/42px-Africa_%28orthographic_projection%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Africa_%28orthographic_projection%29.svg/56px-Africa_%28orthographic_projection%29.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="550" data-file-height="550"></span><span><a href="/wiki/Portal:Africa" title="Portal:Africa">Africa portal</a></span></li>
